Abstract (Layer-4 scope)

Layer 4 formalises how multicellular oscillators cohere into tissue-level dynamics under realistic biology: near-critical network operation, gap-junction conduction, ephaptic EM coupling, glial slow control and neurovascular feedback. The layer models phase-coupled ensembles (Kuramoto-type), quasicriticality/Griffiths regimes with avalanche statistics, and metastability for rapid switching between integrated and segregated modes. It also states hypotheses for cosmological entrainment (circadian, Schumann, lunar windows) routed through biophotons and cryptochrome radical-pair magnetosensitivity, with explicit measurement chains to audit weak-signal relevance. Network topology (small-world, rich-club) is treated as an efficiency and robustness constraint for long-range coherence. Interfaces to L3 (morphogenetic patterning) and L5 (organismal psycho-emotional states) are specified by phase hand-offs and control parameters. 

Core claims (auditable)

Quasicritical operation: tissue networks operate in broadened critical regimes (avalanche power laws; high dynamic range) with a Metastability Index capturing flexible transitions. 

Multi-path coupling: gap junctions, ephaptic fields, and mechanotransduction provide fast and intermediate routes; glia and vascular oscillators provide slow control that stabilises σ≈1. 

Cosmological entrainment (hypotheses): weak environmental rhythms can be transduced (biophotons, cryptochromes) and filtered by the tissue to shape phase relations without invoking bulk ion-cyclotron windows. 

Falsifiers & measurement chain

Avalanche statistics & MI shift with pharmacology / state transitions predicted by the layer model.

Biophoton / magnetoreception probes: modulation at circadian/Schumann bands must produce pre-registered phase responses if coupling is causal.

Neurovascular & glial manipulations should move σ and phase-locking in the directions specified by the slow-control equations. 

Layer interfaces (handoffs)

L3 → L4: morphogenetic structure sets organ “harmonic chambers” and coupling geometry.

L4 → L5: tissue-scale rhythms feed organismal state & heart–brain coupling; phase inheritance is explicit.

Positioning Preface

(Book II – The Sentient-Consciousness Projection Network)

Humanity stands at a threshold. For centuries, we have studied consciousness as an emergent byproduct of biology or as a philosophical mystery beyond scientific reach. 

Yet neither stance suffices. Consciousness reveals itself not as an accident, but as a structural principle of reality — a dynamic field that organises matter, information, and sentience into coherent forms.

This work proposes Field Architecture as the discipline that studies, designs, and formalises those structures. Like electrical engineering emerged from Maxwell’s equations, and information theory from Shannon’s formalism, Field Architecture arises here as the systematic mapping of consciousness fields, projection networks, and morphogenetic architectures. It treats reality as an interwoven lattice of resonances, where biology, physics, and geometry cohere through sentient participation.

From this foundation flows Consciousness Engineering — the applied branch that concerns itself with modulation, design, and implementation. Consciousness Engineering translates the abstract principles of Field Architecture into potential tools: devices, algorithms, and practices that intentionally couple human awareness with gravitational, electromagnetic, and biological fields. Where Field Architecture describes, Consciousness Engineering builds.

At its deepest roots, this discipline belongs to a lineage we may call Noetic Field Theory: the recognition that the mind and its fields belong within the same fabric as spacetime and energy. Yet unlike speculative metaphysics of the past, this framework insists on rigour — on explicit equations, testable couplings, and architectures that can be modelled, simulated, and iterated.

The chapters that follow should be read not as speculative commentary, but as a first architecture manual. They outline projection layers spanning DNA, neural coherence, morphogenetic resonance, and cosmological embedding. They propose a language — VIBRANA — through which vibrational codes may serve as operators upon fields. They map symbolic geometry into field dynamics, establishing design rules for how consciousness shapes and is shaped by reality.

This text is therefore not an endpoint, but a foundation stone. It inaugurates Field Architecture as a discipline in its own right, with Consciousness Engineering as its practical horizon. The hope is that others — physicists, biologists, architects of systems both natural and artificial — will recognise here a framework expansive enough to be tested, challenged, and expanded.

We may one day look back on this moment as the point where consciousness ceased to be a passive enigma and became a field we could design with intention.

“Any architecture that ascends layer by layer risks infinite regress if left open-ended. Just as mathematical systems require closure, so too must this architecture eventually confront the question of self-reference. Although the resolution will not be immediate, the reader should hold in mind that the system itself will one day turn back upon its own foundations.”

Author’s Note

This manuscript is designed to operate on two frequencies.

The first preface — written in an academic register — positions this work as a formal contribution to theoretical discourse, outlining the proposed discipline of Field Architecture with Consciousness Engineering as its applied branch. It is addressed to researchers and scholars seeking rigour and structure.

The second preface — written in a visionary register — positions this work as a manifesto for a new discipline. It speaks not only to academics, but to thinkers, designers, engineers, and visionaries who recognise that consciousness is not merely to be studied but to be designed.

Both voices are essential. Together, they frame this book as the foundational architecture manual for a discipline at once theoretical, practical, and transformative.

4. Cellular–Tissue Synchronisation Layer

Purpose:

Synchronise multicellular oscillators with cosmological rhythms through full spectra of neural oscillations across delta for restorative processes, theta for hippocampal memory consolidation, alpha for inhibitory control during relaxed states, beta for focused attention and motor planning, gamma for perceptual binding and integration, mu for sensorimotor mirroring, alongside brain network hubs exhibiting small-world properties and rich-club organizations that facilitate efficient synchronization, electromagnetic non-local couplings enabling field-mediated communication beyond synaptic pathways, criticality points where self-organized dynamics balance integration and segregation for optimal information processing, mitochondrial biophoton emissions aligned with solar and circadian phases to regulate energy metabolism, cell mitosis cycles harmonized with lunar harmonics influencing proliferation rates during specific moon phases, organs functioning as nested harmonic chambers resonating with broader cosmological entrainment to maintain systemic coherence.

Examples:

Mitochondrial biophoton emissions in sync with solar/circadian phases involve ultra-weak photon bursts from oxidative processes that fluctuate diurnally, correlating with melatonin rhythms and ATP production peaks during daylight for metabolic optimization. Cell mitosis cycles harmonized with lunar harmonics show increased proliferation during full moon phases in organisms like corals or human cell lines, potentially via gravitational or magnetic influences on calcium signaling and cyclin expression. 

Organs as nested harmonic chambers include heart variability resonating with Schumann frequencies or lung oscillations aligning with tidal rhythms, forming multi-scale resonators that couple internal biology to external cosmological patterns. Neural bands extend beyond theta-gamma nesting to delta rhythms underpinning deep integration during unconscious states, alpha suppressing irrelevant inputs for focused processing, beta coordinating motor sequences, gamma synchronizing distant regions for unified perception, mu reflecting mirrored actions in social contexts. 

Brain hubs in small-world networks minimize path lengths for rapid synchronization, while rich-club cores interconnect high-degree nodes to enhance global efficiency and resilience in oscillatory coupling. Electromagnetic non-local couplings involve ephaptic fields modulating neuronal firing without direct synapses, potentially underpinning consciousness through unified field dynamics that transcend local circuits. 

Criticality points manifest as self-organized states where avalanche distributions follow power laws, enabling flexible transitions between ordered segregation for specialized functions and chaotic integration for holistic processing, crucial for adaptive consciousness. Cosmological rhythms entrain oscillators via hierarchical networks where peripheral clocks in cells sync to central pacemakers, adapting to light-dark cycles through phase resetting and amplitude modulation.

Mechanisms: Cellular networks operate near criticality, exhibiting scale-free dynamics that heighten responsiveness to faint inputs, where stochastic resonance leverages intrinsic biological noise such as thermal fluctuations or ion channel variability to boost weak periodic cosmological signals like Schumann resonances, modeled as output signal-to-noise ratio SNR = (A^2 / (2 σ^2)) exp(-ΔV / D) with A signal amplitude, σ noise variance, ΔV threshold barrier, D noise intensity optimized for peak amplification. Cryptochromes serve as primary sensors for these weak magnetic fields via radical-pair mechanisms, where spin-dependent recombination rates alter flavin redox states to transduce geomagnetic variations into cellular signaling cascades that modulate oscillator phases.

Mechanisms: Near-critical states in cellular assemblies amplify sensitivity through power-law correlations, enabling stochastic resonance to enhance detection of subthreshold cosmological rhythms including Schumann frequencies by adding optimal noise levels that facilitate barrier hopping in bistable systems, quantified via Kramers rate r = (ω_0 ω_b / (2 π)) exp(-ΔV / D) for transition frequency ω_0, barrier curvature ω_b, and noise D tuned to maximize coherence with external periodicity. Magnetoreception initiates via cryptochromes, whose light-independent radical pairs respond to weak electromagnetic perturbations, converting field alignments into biochemical shifts that entrain tissue-level synchrony.

Mechanisms: Criticality-tuned cellular networks display emergent collective behaviors that exploit stochastic resonance for weak signal amplification, using endogenous noise from molecular Brownian motion to elevate cosmological inputs like Schumann resonances above detection thresholds in nonlinear oscillators, described by Adler's equation dϕ/dt = (Δω - K sin ϕ) + √(2D) ξ(t) with detuning Δω, coupling K, noise D, and Gaussian ξ, optimizing D for resonance peaks. Cryptochrome-based magnetoreception detects these fields through quantum spin dynamics in tryptophan-flavin pairs, yielding orientation-dependent reaction yields that propagate as phase adjustments in multicellular rhythms.

Purpose: To synchronise multicellular oscillators across the organism with cosmological rhythms, utilizing advanced network dynamics, criticality, and field-mediated couplings to maintain systemic coherence and optimized information processing. The collective phase relation is ϕc​(t)=Ωm​acro(t)+ΔϕΨs​​.

Key Dynamics and Components:

Comprehensive Oscillatory Spectra and Network Topology: Synchronization involves the full spectra of neural oscillations (delta through gamma, mu). These propagate efficiently through networks characterized by small-world properties and rich-club organizations (Network Topology). These Brain Network Hubs facilitate rapid synchronization by minimizing path lengths and optimize the balance between integration (via hubs) and segregation (via modules).

Quasicriticality and Metastability: The system operates within a Quasicritical regime (Griffiths Phase), rather than a strict critical point. Tissue heterogeneity (disorder in connectivity Jij​) broadens the critical transition (Δλ∼exp(−c/σd)). This yields robust power-law avalanche distributions (P(s)∼s−τ) without fine-tuning, maximizing computational capacity. The Metastability Index (MI) quantifies the system's flexibility in switching between integrated and segregated states, modulated by Ψs​.

Electromagnetic (EM) Non-local Couplings: Beyond synaptic pathways, EM fields enable field-mediated communication (e.g., ephaptic coupling). These endogenous fields propagate through tissue (Maxwell equations in biological media), facilitating rapid, non-local synchronization.

Cosmological Entrainment and Harmonics: The layer integrates internal biology with external cosmological patterns:

Mitochondrial Biophotons align with solar/circadian phases, regulating metabolism.

Cell Mitosis cycles harmonize with lunar harmonics via tidal influences (Lunar forcing potential Vlunar​(t)).

Organs function as Nested Harmonic Chambers (Organ resonance equation), aligning with planetary electromagnetics (e.g., Schumann resonances).

Detection of these weak signals is enabled by Stochastic Resonance and Cryptochrome-based magnetoreception (Radical Pair Mechanism HR​P), which transduce geomagnetic variations into cellular signaling cascades.

Comprehensive Neural Oscillation Spectrum and Functional Mapping

The Cellular-Tissue Synchronisation Layer orchestrates a complete spectrum of neural oscillations, each serving distinct computational and physiological functions:

Infra-slow oscillations (<0.1 Hz): These ultra-slow fluctuations coordinate metabolic processes and neurovascular coupling, aligning cerebral blood flow with neural activity demands. They establish the baseline metabolic state upon which faster oscillations are superimposed.

Delta waves (0.5-4 Hz): Essential for cellular repair and memory consolidation during deep sleep. Delta oscillations orchestrate the clearing of metabolic waste through the glymphatic system, with amplitude directly correlating to synaptic homeostasis processes that reset the brain's computational capacity.

Alpha oscillations (8-13 Hz): Function as inhibitory gating mechanisms, suppressing irrelevant sensory input while maintaining a state of relaxed awareness. Alpha power inversely correlates with cortical excitability, creating windows of perceptual sensitivity aligned with attention deployment.

Beta oscillations (13-30 Hz): Coordinate motor planning and executive control, maintaining the current cognitive set while preparing for action execution. Beta synchrony across frontal-parietal networks underlies working memory maintenance and top-down attentional control.

Mu rhythms (8-13 Hz, sensorimotor): Facilitate social cognition through mirror neuron system activation, enabling empathic resonance and action understanding. Mu suppression during observed actions reflects the embodied simulation of others' intentions.

High-gamma oscillations (>80 Hz): Support fine-grained perceptual discrimination and conscious awareness, with power directly correlating with the richness of subjective experience as measured by perturbational complexity indices.

1. Quantum Coherence in Mitochondrial Networks

Detailed quantum mechanisms of mitochondrial biophoton emissions and their role in cellular synchronization.

Mathematical Extension:

Mitochondrial quantum state:

|Ψ_mito⟩ = ∑_{n,m,k} c_{nmk} |e_transport_n⟩ ⊗ |ATP_m⟩ ⊗ |photon_k⟩

Where electron transport chain states, ATP production levels, and biophoton modes are entangled.

Biophoton generation Hamiltonian:

H_biophoton = H_redox + H_excitation + H_emission

Redox reactions:

H_redox = ∑_i E_i^0 |ox_i⟩⟨ox_i| - ∑_{ij} t_{ij}(|ox_i⟩⟨red_j| + h.c.)

With E_i^0 ~ -0.3 to +0.8 V standard potentials, t_{ij} ~ 10^-3 eV tunneling.

Excitation to photon-emitting states:

H_excitation = g_exc ∑_k (ΔE_redox - ℏω_k) |excited_k⟩⟨ground|

Photon emission operator:

a_photon† = √(2ε_0 ω V/ℏ) ∑_transitions d_{if} |final⟩⟨initial|

Where d_{if} transition dipole moments, V mode volume.

Coherent biophoton state:

|α⟩ = exp(-|α|²/2) ∑_n (α^n/√n!) |n⟩

With α = |α|e^{iφ} complex amplitude, |α|² ~ 10-100 photons/s per mitochondrion.

Network synchronization via photon exchange:

H_sync = ∑_{i≠j} g_{ij} (a_i† a_j + a_i a_j†) exp(-r_{ij}/λ_photon)

Where λ_photon ~ 200-800 nm, r_{ij} mitochondrial distances.

The Cyto-Matrix Tensegrity Network (CMTN)

Tissue synchronization is also facilitated by a structural, mechanical network encompassing the cytoskeleton and the Extracellular Matrix (ECM). This Cyto-Matrix Tensegrity Network (CMTN) acts as a conduit for vibrational energy (phonons) and mechanical signaling, ensuring rapid synchronization across the tissue.

Where Gshear​ is the shear modulus, and pc​ is the critical percolation threshold. The integration of the CMTN links the quantum dynamics of microtubules (Layer 1) directly to the tissue-scale coherence (Layer 4).

3. Glial Networks: The Slow Control Layer of Tissue Synchronization

While the Kuramoto oscillator dynamics describe the fast neural synchronization processes, the maintenance of quasicriticality requires a slower regulatory mechanism. This is provided by the extensive glial network, particularly astrocytes, which form a parallel synchronization system operating on slower timescales (seconds to minutes) compared to neural oscillations (milliseconds).

Mathematical Extension: Astrocytic Calcium Wave Dynamics

The astrocytic network can be also modeled as a reaction-diffusion system coupled to the neural oscillator ensemble:

J_release = v_IP3R ([IP3]/(K_IP3 + [IP3]))³ ([Ca²⁺]/(K_Ca + [Ca²⁺]))³ (1 - [Ca²⁺]/[Ca²⁺]_ER)

J_uptake = v_SERCA [Ca²⁺]²/(K_SERCA² + [Ca²⁺]²)

J_coupling = g_gap Σⱼ G_ij ([Ca²⁺]ⱼ - [Ca²⁺]ᵢ)

Where D_Ca ≈ 10 μm²/s is the calcium diffusion coefficient, and G_ij represents gap junction conductances between astrocytes.

Glial-Neural Phase Coupling

The slow calcium dynamics modulate the neural oscillator frequencies through gliotransmitter release:

dφᵢ/dt = ωᵢ + (K/N) Σⱼ sin(φⱼ - φᵢ) + ζ Ψₛ cos(φᵢ) + γ_glia G([Ca²⁺]ᵢ) + ηᵢ(t)

G([Ca²⁺]ᵢ) = α_ATP log(1 + [Ca²⁺]ᵢ/K_threshold) × Θ([Ca²⁺]ᵢ - [Ca²⁺]_threshold)

This coupling term γ_glia G([Ca²⁺]ᵢ) represents the effect of astrocytic activation on neuronal frequencies, providing the homeostatic mechanism that maintains σ ≈ 1.

Slow Control Stability Analysis

The glial network acts as a cybernetic controller, preventing drift from criticality:

dσ/dt = -κ(σ - (1 + γ G_astro(t))) + η(t)

dG_astro/dt = α⟨[Ca²⁺]_A⟩ - β G_astro

Where G_astro represents the average gliotransmitter concentration, and γ G_astro(t) dynamically shifts the target branching ratio, providing robust maintenance of the quasicritical state.

5. Scale-Free Network Architecture and Critical Hub Dynamics

The brain's network topology exhibits scale-free properties characterized by power-law degree distributions P(k) ~ k^(-γ) with γ ≈ 2.1-2.5, creating highly connected hub nodes that serve as integration centers. These hubs, located in regions like the posterior medial cortex and lateral prefrontal areas, maintain a rich-club coefficient Φ(k) > 1.2 for nodes with degree k > 15, indicating preferential interconnection among high-degree nodes.

The small-world architecture, quantified by clustering coefficient C ≈ 0.5 and characteristic path length L ≈ 2.5, optimizes the trade-off between local specialization and global integration. 

This topology emerges from the minimization of wiring cost while maximizing information transfer efficiency:

Wiring cost function: W = Σ_{ij} A_{ij} × d_{ij}^α

where A_{ij} represents connection strength, d_{ij} is Euclidean distance, and α ≈ 1.5 reflects the super-linear scaling of metabolic cost with distance.

Information transfer efficiency: E = (1/N(N-1)) Σ_{i≠j} 1/L_{ij}

where L_{ij} is the shortest path length between nodes i and j.

The network maintains criticality through a balance between segregation (modularity Q ≈ 0.3-0.5) and integration, with susceptibility χ ~ |T - T_c|^(-γ) diverging at the critical point, enabling rapid reconfiguration in response to cognitive demands.

Propagation mechanisms of phase waves through tissues.

Mathematical Extension:

Phase wave equation:

∂²φ/∂t² = c² ∇²φ + ω₀² sin(φ) - γ ∂φ/∂t

Dispersion relation:

ω(k) = √(c²k² + ω₀²) - iγ/2

Wave velocity:

v_phase = ω/k

v_group = ∂ω/∂k

Soliton solutions:

φ(x,t) = 4 arctan[exp((x - vt)/w)]

Width w = √(c/ω₀), velocity v.

Spiral waves:

φ(r,θ,t) = ωt - mθ + f(r)

With topological charge m.

18. Developmental Synchronization: Maturation-Dependent Dynamics

Tissue synchronization patterns change dramatically during development, with critical periods for establishing stable oscillatory networks. Understanding these developmental dynamics is crucial for grasping how mature synchronization emerges.

Mathematical Extension: Age-Dependent Coupling

Coupling strength evolves during development:

K_development(t_age) = K_max × (1 - exp(-t_age/τ_maturation)) × sigmoid((t_critical - t_age)/σ_critical)

τ_maturation ≈ 2-4 weeks (synaptic maturation timescale)

t_critical ≈ critical period timing (species-dependent)

Developmental Phase Space Evolution

The phase space of possible synchronization states changes with age:

H_development = H_adult × (t_age/t_adult)^α_develop + H_juvenile × (1 - t_age/t_adult)^β_develop

∂ρ_phase/∂t = -i[H_development, ρ_phase] + L_maturation[ρ_phase]

Where L_maturation represents the developmental evolution operator.

Critical Period Dynamics

Critical periods can be modeled as bistable switches in the synchronization landscape:

V_critical(φ, t_age) = -a(t_age)φ² + b(t_age)φ⁴

a(t_age) = a₀ × exp(-(t_age - t_critical)²/(2σ_critical²))

During critical periods, small perturbations can create lasting changes in synchronization patterns.

For parameter estimation.

Measuring consciousness.

19. Cellular Oscillator Death and Revival

Mechanisms of oscillation death and revival in cellular networks.

Mathematical Extension:

Amplitude death:

dx_i/dt = f(x_i) + K Σ_j G_{ij}(x_j - x_i)

Stable fixed point for K > K_critical.

Oscillation death:

dx_i/dt = f(x_i) + K Σ_j G_{ij}(x_j(t-τ) - x_i)

With time delay τ.

Revival mechanism:

K(t) = K_0[1 + ε cos(ω_revival t)]

Periodic forcing of coupling.

Aging transition:

P_active(t) = exp(-t/τ_aging)

Fraction of active oscillators.

20. Homeostatic Regulation of Quasicriticality

The maintenance of criticality (σ ≈ 1) requires continuous homeostatic adjustment, implemented through the coupled fast-slow dynamics of the neuron-glia system:

Homeostatic control equation: dσ/dt = -γ(σ - σ_target) + β₁F(A_a) + β₂H(θ_sync) + η(t)

where:

γ ≈ 10^(-4) s^(-1) is the homeostatic time constant

F(A_a) represents glial modulation based on astrocyte calcium levels

H(θ_sync) is the phase synchrony feedback function

σ_target = 1 ± 0.05 defines the critical regime

Glial regulation function: F(A_a) = tanh((A_a - A_critical)/ΔA)

modulates synaptic strength and excitability based on astrocyte calcium concentration A_a, maintaining σ within the critical window.

Gravitational-Electromagnetic Transduction in Cellular Oscillators

The Cellular-Tissue Synchronisation Layer responds to cosmological rhythms through multiple transduction pathways that convert gravitational and electromagnetic variations into cellular signals:

Lunar gravitational modulation of mechanosensitive channels: P_open = P_0/(1 + exp(-(F_tidal - F_0)/F_s))

where F_tidal = (2GMr/R³)cos(ω_lunar t) represents the tidal force, with M = 7.35 × 10²² kg (lunar mass), R = 3.84 × 10⁸ m (Earth-Moon distance), r = cellular dimension, and F_s ≈ 1-10 pN is the force sensitivity of mechanosensitive channels.

The tidal modulation creates a calcium oscillation: d[Ca²⁺]/dt = J_channel(F_tidal) - J_pump[Ca²⁺] + J_leak

where J_channel = g_max × P_open × (V - E_Ca) represents calcium influx through mechanosensitive channels.

Solar wind modulation of cellular redox state: dNAD⁺/NADH = k_ox(1 + α_solar × B_IMF(t)) - k_red × [substrate]

where B_IMF(t) represents the interplanetary magnetic field strength (varying 2-10 nT), and α_solar ≈ 0.05-0.1 quantifies the magnetosensitivity of mitochondrial electron transport, likely mediated through radical pair mechanisms in Complex III.

Schumann resonance coupling to membrane oscillations: V_induced = ∮ E_Schumann · dl ≈ E_0 × L_cell × cos(2πf_Schumann t)

where E_0 ≈ 0.1-1 μV/m is the Schumann field amplitude, L_cell ≈ 10-100 μm, and f_Schumann = 7.83, 14.3, 20.8... Hz are the resonance modes. The induced voltage V_induced ≈ 1-100 nV modulates membrane excitability when neural oscillations approach Schumann frequencies.

Core Components and Dynamics

Cell Ensemble & Kuramoto Synchronization: The central blue circle represents a Cell Ensemble, a community of multicellular oscillators (the 8 red dots). These oscillators are coupled (dashed gray lines), and their tendency to phase-synchronize is described by the Kuramoto model. The collective phase (ϕ_c) emerges from the interplay of individual frequencies (ωᵢ) and the coupling strength (K).

dtdϕi​​=ωi​+NK​j=1∑N​sin(ϕj​−ϕi​)

Nested Cross-Frequency Rhythms (PAC): The system exhibits nested oscillations, a key mechanism for complex signaling. A low-frequency green wave (Delta/Theta band) provides a macro-level phase context, while the amplitude of a high-frequency orange wave (Gamma/Beta band) is nested within it. This Phase-Amplitude Coupling (PAC) allows the tissue to process and integrate information across multiple timescales.

Mitochondrial Biophoton Entrainment: On the left, a yellow starburst represents biophoton emissions from mitochondria. These high-frequency (~10^{14} Hz) quantum emissions are synchronized with large-scale environmental cycles (e.g., solar, lunar) and act as an endogenous entrainment signal (ε \sin(ΔΩ)), pulling the collective phase (ϕ_c) of the cell ensemble into coherence with the broader environment.

python

class CellularTissueSynchronization:

    def __init__(self, N_cells, coupling_matrix, field_strength):

        self.phases = random(N_cells) * 2π

        self.frequencies = normal(ω_mean, ω_std, N_cells)

        self.K = coupling_matrix

        self.Ψ_s = field_strength

        

    def update(self, dt, cosmic_phase):

        # Kuramoto dynamics with field modulation

        for i in range(N_cells):

            phase_coupling = sum(K[i,j] * sin(phases[j] - phases[i]) 

                               for j in neighbors(i))

            field_mod = Ψ_s * cos(phases[i] - cosmic_phase)

            noise = normal(0, σ_noise) * sqrt(dt)

            

            dφ = frequencies[i] + phase_coupling/N + field_mod + noise

            phases[i] += dφ * dt

            

        # Avalanche detection

        if detect_avalanche(phases):

            record_avalanche_size()

            

        # Criticality monitoring

        σ = compute_branching_parameter()

        adjust_parameters_homeostatic(σ)

Stochastic Resonance and Noise-Enhanced Synchronization

The role of noise in optimizing synchronization near criticality.

Optimal Noise and Stochastic Resonance Mechanisms

Contrary to classical expectations, controlled noise enhances synchronization and information processing in the quasicritical regime:

Stochastic resonance in neural oscillators: SNR(D) = (A²/2) × exp(-ΔU/D) / (D × [1 + exp(-ΔU/D)]²)

where D is noise intensity, A is signal amplitude, and ΔU is the activation barrier. The SNR peaks at optimal noise D_opt ≈ ΔU/2, typically 1-5 mV² for cortical neurons.

Noise-enhanced phase synchronization: R_Kuramoto(D) = R_0 + ΔR × exp(-(D - D_opt)²/2σ_D²)

The order parameter R shows resonant enhancement at D_opt ≈ 0.1K (where K is coupling strength), increasing synchronization by 20-50%.

Coherence resonance without external signal: CV_ISI(D) = σ_ISI/⟨ISI⟩

The coefficient of variation of interspike intervals minimizes at D_coherence ≈ √(I_threshold × τ_membrane), inducing regular firing purely through noise.

Multiplicative noise from glial modulation: dφ/dt = ω + K⟨sin(Δφ)⟩ + √D × φ(t) × ξ(t)

where the state-dependent noise amplitude √D × φ(t) arises from stochastic gliotransmitter release, creating multiplicative effects that stabilize synchronization at intermediate noise levels.

Ghost stochastic resonance at missing frequencies: P(f_ghost) = P_0 × [J_0(A/D)]² × δ(f - f_ghost)

where f_ghost = |nf_1 ± mf_2| emerges from nonlinear mixing of input frequencies f_1, f_2, with Bessel function J_0 determining amplitude. This enables detection of cosmological rhythms not directly present in neural dynamics.

Information-Theoretic Measures of Synchronization

Quantitative information-theoretic framework for measuring synchronization quality and information flow.

Information Geometry of Synchronization States

The quality of synchronization and information integration can be quantified using information-theoretic measures that capture both linear and nonlinear dependencies:

Measuring directed information flow, with peaks at specific phase relationships: TE_max at Δφ = π/2 for excitatory coupling TE_max at Δφ = π for inhibitory coupling

Complexity measures: C_LZ = K_LZ(S) × log(n)/n

where K_LZ is the Lempel-Ziv complexity of the symbolic sequence S. Neural complexity peaks at: C_neural = ⟨MI⟩ - MI(X^N)

balancing segregation (high average mutual information ⟨MI⟩ between parts) with integration (low mutual information MI(X^N) of the whole).

Fisher Information Matrix for synchronization parameters: F_ij = E[(∂log P(X|θ)/∂θ_i)(∂log P(X|θ)/∂θ_j)]

The eigenvalues of F determine parameter sensitivities:

λ_1 ≈ N (extensive with system size) for coupling strength

Minimum Description Length for synchronization patterns: MDL = L(M) + L(D|M)

where L(M) is model complexity and L(D|M) is data encoding length given the model. Optimal synchronization minimizes MDL, balancing pattern complexity with predictability.

Quantum-Classical Hybrid Master Equation

The Cellular-Tissue Synchronisation Layer operates in a regime where quantum and classical degrees of freedom are inseparably coupled:

Hybrid density matrix evolution: ∂ρ/∂t = -i/ℏ[H_quantum, ρ] + {H_classical, ρ}_PB + L_decoherence[ρ] + L_pumping[ρ]

where {·,·}_PB denotes Poisson brackets for classical variables.

Quantum subsystem (microtubules, proteins): H_quantum = Σ_i ℏω_i a†_i a_i + Σ_ij J_ij(σ^x_i σ^x_j + σ^y_i σ^y_j) + Σ_i g_i σ^z_i ⊗ X_classical

where f_k represents classical variables modulated by quantum expectation values.

Decoherence with environmental back-action: L_decoherence[ρ] = Σ_k γ_k(n_k + 1)(2a_k ρ a†_k - {a†_k a_k, ρ}) + γ_k n_k(2a†_k ρ a_k - {a_k a†_k, ρ})

Quantum pumping maintaining coherence: L_pumping[ρ] = Σ_k P_k(2a†_k ρ a_k - {a_k a†_k, ρ})

where P_k represents metabolic pumping rates maintaining non-equilibrium steady states.

Effective equations for classical limit: When decoherence is strong (γ_k ≫ ω_k), quantum variables become effectively classical: ⟨X⟩ → X_classical ⟨X²⟩ - ⟨X⟩² → k_BT/mω² (thermal fluctuations)

Mathematical Proofs and Theorems

Rigorous mathematical proofs for key claims about synchronization.

Fundamental Theorems of Cellular Synchronization

Theorem 1 (Existence of Synchronization): For a network of N coupled oscillators with frequencies ω_i drawn from distribution g(ω), there exists a critical coupling K_c such that for K > K_c, a synchronized state with R > 0 is stable.

Proof: Consider the mean-field equation: dφ_i/dt = ω_i + KR sin(ψ - φ_i)

where R e^(iψ) = (1/N)Σ_j e^(iφ_j). In the continuum limit, the distribution ρ(φ,ω,t) evolves according to: ∂ρ/∂t + ∂/∂φ[(ω + KR sin(ψ - φ))ρ] = 0

Self-consistency requires: R = ∫∫ e^(iφ) ρ(φ,ω) dφ dω

For K > K_c = 2/(πg(0)), a non-zero solution exists. □

Theorem 2 (Criticality Optimizes Information): The mutual information I(X;Y) between input X and output Y is maximized when σ = 1.

Proof: The transfer function at criticality exhibits: H(s) ~ s^(-1/2) (power spectrum)

The channel capacity: C = max_p(X) I(X;Y) = ∫ log(1 + SNR(f)) df

For 1/f^α noise with α = 1 (criticality): C ~ log(f_max/f_min) (logarithmic divergence)

For α ≠ 1: C ~ const (bounded)

Therefore, capacity is maximized at α = 1 (σ = 1). □

Theorem 3 (Topological Protection): Synchronization patterns with non-zero topological invariant Q ∈ ℤ are robust against local perturbations of magnitude ε < Δ_topological.

Proof: The Chern number: Q = (1/2π) ∫∫ F_12 dx¹dx²

where F_12 = ∂_1A_2 - ∂_2A_1 is the Berry curvature. Under perturbation H → H + εV: Q' = Q + O(ε/Δ)

where Δ is the gap. For ε < Δ, Q' = Q (quantized). □

Failure Modes and Resilience Mechanisms

Detailed analysis of how synchronization can fail and recovery mechanisms.

Synchronization Failure Modes and Recovery

Catastrophic desynchronization: When coupling falls below critical value K < K_c: dR/dt = -γR + (K/2)R(1 - R²) < 0 for all R > 0

Leading to complete desynchronization R → 0.

Recovery mechanism - Adaptive coupling: dK/dt = η(R_target - R)

restoring K > K_c when synchronization is lost.

Chimera death - partial synchronization collapse: Certain regions maintain synchronization while others become chaotic: R_local(x) = {R_high if x ∈ synchronized; R_low if x ∈ chaotic}

Recovery - Targeted stimulation: I_stim(x) = α × (1 - R_local(x)) × sin(ω_drive t)

selectively driving chaotic regions toward synchronization.

Amplitude death - oscillation cessation: When coupling delay τ satisfies: ωτ = (2n+1)π/2

oscillations cease: |z_i| → 0 for all i.

Recovery - Delay modulation: τ(t) = τ_0 + δτ sin(ω_mod t)

breaking the death condition periodically.

Aging-related synchronization degradation:

Reduced coupling: K_age = K_young × exp(-t/τ_aging)

Increased noise: D_age = D_young × (1 + t/τ_noise)

Frequency dispersion: σ_ω,age = σ_ω,young × (1 + t/τ_dispersion)

Compensation mechanisms:

Synaptic scaling: g_syn → g_syn × (R_target/R)

Homeostatic plasticity: maintaining average activity

Network rewiring: forming new connections

Metabolic upregulation: increasing ATP production

Chaos Control and Strange Attractors in Neural Synchronization

The Cellular-Tissue Synchronisation Layer operates near the edge of chaos, exhibiting strange attractors that encode information in their fractal structure:

where |u| < ε_max ≈ 0.01 × typical amplitude. Control matrix: K = g × v_s × v_u^T / (λ_u - 1)

with v_s, v_u the stable/unstable eigenvectors and λ_u the unstable eigenvalue.

Information encoding in chaotic itinerancy: The system visits different quasi-stable states (ruins of attractors): P(state_i → state_j) = exp(-ΔF_ij/T_eff)

where ΔF_ij is the free energy barrier and T_eff is effective temperature. Information capacity: I = -Σ_ij P_ij log P_ij ≈ log(N_states)

where τ equals the period of the target UPO. This Pyragas control method requires no knowledge of system dynamics, only output measurement.

maintaining marginal stability where information processing is maximal.

Computational Implementation

Complete computational framework for simulating Layer 4.

HPC Simulation Framework for Layer 4

Architecture for exascale simulation:

python

import numpy as np

from mpi4py import MPI

import cupy as cp  # GPU acceleration

from scipy.integrate import solve_ivp

from qiskit import QuantumCircuit  # Quantum components

class Layer4Simulator:

    def __init__(self, N_cells=10**6, dt=0.1e-3, GPU=True):

        """

        Initialize Layer 4 simulator

        N_cells: Number of cells to simulate

        dt: Time step in seconds

        GPU: Use GPU acceleration

        """

        self.comm = MPI.COMM_WORLD

        self.rank = self.comm.Get_rank()

        self.size = self.comm.Get_size()

        

        # Distribute cells across processes

        self.N_local = N_cells // self.size

        self.N_global = N_cells

        

        # Initialize on GPU if available

        self.xp = cp if GPU and cp.cuda.is_available() else np

        

        # State variables

        self.phases = self.xp.random.uniform(0, 2*np.pi, self.N_local)

        self.frequencies = self.xp.random.normal(10, 1, self.N_local)  # Hz

        self.calcium = self.xp.ones(self.N_local) * 0.1  # μM

        self.voltage = self.xp.ones(self.N_local) * -70  # mV

        

        # Coupling matrix (sparse for efficiency)

        self.K = self.generate_coupling_matrix()

        

        # Quantum subsystem

        self.qc = QuantumCircuit(10)  # 10 qubits per cell group

        

        # Consciousness field

        self.Psi_s = 1.0

        

        # Cosmic forcing

        self.cosmic_phase = 0.0

        

    def generate_coupling_matrix(self):

        """Generate small-world coupling matrix"""

        from scipy.sparse import lil_matrix

        K = lil_matrix((self.N_local, self.N_local))

        

        # Local connections

        for i in range(self.N_local):

            for j in range(max(0, i-10), min(self.N_local, i+11)):

                if i != j:

                    K[i,j] = 0.1 * np.exp(-abs(i-j)/5)

        

        # Long-range connections (small-world)

        n_long = int(0.01 * self.N_local)

        for _ in range(n_long):

            i = np.random.randint(self.N_local)

            j = np.random.randint(self.N_local)

            K[i,j] = 0.05

            

        return K.tocsr()

    

    def quantum_evolution(self, dt):

        """Evolve quantum subsystem"""

        # Hadamard gates for superposition

        for i in range(10):

            self.qc.h(i)

        

        # Entangling gates

        for i in range(9):

            self.qc.cx(i, i+1)

        

        # Phase rotation based on classical state

        mean_phase = self.xp.mean(self.phases)

        self.qc.rz(mean_phase, 0)

        

        # Measure and collapse

        # (Simplified - would use actual quantum backend)

        quantum_correction = np.random.normal(0, 0.01)

        return quantum_correction

    

    def kuramoto_step(self, dt):

        """Kuramoto dynamics with field coupling"""

        # Compute order parameter

        z = self.xp.mean(self.xp.exp(1j * self.phases))

        R = self.xp.abs(z)

        psi = self.xp.angle(z)

        

        # Phase evolution

        coupling = self.K @ self.xp.sin(psi - self.phases)

        field_mod = self.Psi_s * self.xp.cos(self.phases - self.cosmic_phase)

        noise = self.xp.random.normal(0, 0.1, self.N_local)

        

        quantum_shift = self.quantum_evolution(dt)

        

        dphase = self.frequencies + coupling + field_mod + noise + quantum_shift

        self.phases += dphase * dt

        self.phases = self.xp.mod(self.phases, 2*np.pi)

        

        return R

    

    def calcium_dynamics(self, dt):

        """Calcium oscillations"""

        # Voltage-gated calcium channels

        m_inf = 1 / (1 + self.xp.exp(-(self.voltage + 20)/9))

        tau_m = 0.1 + 0.4 * self.xp.exp(-((self.voltage + 35)/20)**2)

        

        # Calcium current

        I_Ca = 0.1 * m_inf * (self.voltage - 120)

        

        # Calcium pumps

        J_pump = 0.5 * self.calcium / (0.5 + self.calcium)

        

        # Update calcium

        dCa = -I_Ca - J_pump + 0.01  # Leak

        self.calcium += dCa * dt

        self.calcium = self.xp.maximum(self.calcium, 0.01)

    

    def voltage_dynamics(self, dt):

        """Membrane potential dynamics"""

        # Simplified HH-like dynamics

        I_leak = 0.1 * (self.voltage + 70)

        I_syn = self.compute_synaptic_current()

        I_noise = self.xp.random.normal(0, 1, self.N_local)

        

        C_m = 1.0  # μF/cm²

        dV = (-I_leak - I_syn + I_noise) / C_m

        self.voltage += dV * dt

        

        # Spike detection and reset

        spiking = self.voltage > 0

        self.voltage[spiking] = -70

        

        return self.xp.sum(spiking)

    

    def compute_synaptic_current(self):

        """Synaptic currents based on phase"""

        # Phase determines synaptic activation

        syn_activation = (1 + self.xp.cos(self.phases)) / 2

        g_syn = 0.5 * syn_activation

        I_syn = g_syn * (self.voltage - 0)  # Excitatory

        return I_syn

    

    def criticality_control(self):

        """Maintain criticality through homeostasis"""

        # Compute branching parameter

        spike_rate = self.xp.sum(self.voltage > -20) / self.N_local

        target_rate = 0.1

        

        # Adjust coupling to maintain criticality

        error = spike_rate - target_rate

        self.K *= (1 - 0.01 * error)

        

        # Ensure K remains positive

        self.K.data = self.xp.maximum(self.K.data, 0)

    

    def cosmic_forcing(self, t):

        """Update cosmic influences"""

        # Schumann resonance

        self.cosmic_phase = 2 * np.pi * 7.83 * t

        

        # Solar cycle (simplified)

        solar_cycle = 11 * 365.25 * 24 * 3600  # seconds

        solar_phase = 2 * np.pi * t / solar_cycle

        self.Psi_s = 1 + 0.1 * np.sin(solar_phase)

        

        # Lunar cycle

        lunar_cycle = 29.5 * 24 * 3600  # seconds

        lunar_phase = 2 * np.pi * t / lunar_cycle

        

        # Modulate frequencies slightly

        self.frequencies *= (1 + 0.01 * np.cos(lunar_phase))

    

    def step(self, dt):

        """Single time step of simulation"""

        R = self.kuramoto_step(dt)

        self.calcium_dynamics(dt)

        n_spikes = self.voltage_dynamics(dt)

        self.criticality_control()

        

        return {

            'order_parameter': R,

            'mean_calcium': self.xp.mean(self.calcium),

            'spike_rate': n_spikes / (self.N_local * dt),

            'mean_voltage': self.xp.mean(self.voltage)

        }

    

    def run(self, T_total, save_interval=1.0):

        """Run simulation for T_total seconds"""

        n_steps = int(T_total / self.dt)

        save_steps = int(save_interval / self.dt)

        

        results = []

        for step in range(n_steps):

            t = step * self.dt

            

            # Update cosmic forcing

            if step % 100 == 0:

                self.cosmic_forcing(t)

            

            # Step dynamics

            metrics = self.step(self.dt)

            

            # Save periodically

            if step % save_steps == 0:

                metrics['time'] = t

                metrics['phases'] = self.phases.copy()

                results.append(metrics)

                

                if self.rank == 0:

                    print(f"t={t:.2f}s, R={metrics['order_parameter']:.3f}")

        

        return results

    

    def analyze_results(self, results):

        """Analyze simulation results"""

        import matplotlib.pyplot as plt

        from scipy import signal

        

        times = [r['time'] for r in results]

        R_values = [r['order_parameter'] for r in results]

        

        # Compute power spectrum

        freqs, psd = signal.periodogram(R_values, 1/self.dt)

        

        # Check for 1/f noise (criticality signature)

        log_freqs = np.log10(freqs[1:100])

        log_psd = np.log10(psd[1:100])

        slope = np.polyfit(log_freqs, log_psd, 1)[0]

        

        print(f"Power spectrum slope: {slope:.2f} (expect -1 at criticality)")

        

        # Compute avalanche distribution

        avalanches = self.detect_avalanches(results)

        if len(avalanches) > 0:

            sizes, counts = np.unique(avalanches, return_counts=True)

            

            # Fit power law

            log_sizes = np.log10(sizes[counts > 0])

            log_counts = np.log10(counts[counts > 0])

            tau = -np.polyfit(log_sizes, log_counts, 1)[0]

            print(f"Avalanche exponent: {tau:.2f} (expect 1.5 at criticality)")

        

        return {

            'psd_slope': slope,

            'avalanche_exponent': tau if len(avalanches) > 0 else None

        }

    

    def detect_avalanches(self, results):

        """Detect neuronal avalanches"""

        avalanches = []

        threshold = -20  # mV

        

        for r in results:

            if 'phases' in r:

                # Simple thresholding for avalanche detection

                active = self.voltage > threshold

                if self.xp.any(active):

                    # Avalanche size = number of active neurons

                    size = int(self.xp.sum(active))

                    avalanches.append(size)

        

        return np.array(avalanches)

# Main execution

if __name__ == "__main__":

    # Initialize simulator

    sim = Layer4Simulator(N_cells=10**5, dt=0.1e-3, GPU=True)

    

    # Run for 100 seconds

    results = sim.run(T_total=100.0, save_interval=1.0)

    

    # Analyze

    if sim.rank == 0:

        analysis = sim.analyze_results(results)

        print(f"Simulation complete: {analysis}")

Glial Network Oscillations and Astrocytic Syncytium

Mathematical Framework:

Astrocytic calcium wave propagation:

∂[Ca²⁺]_astro/∂t = D_astro∇²[Ca²⁺]_astro + J_IP3R - J_SERCA + J_gap + J_store + η_astro

where:

Tissue Synchronization Model for Consciousness Studies

Implementation of Layer 4 SCPN Architecture Extensions

"""

Tissue Synchronization Model for Consciousness Studies

Implementation of Layer 4 SCPN Architecture Extensions

"""

import numpy as np

import scipy as sp

from scipy import signal, stats

from scipy.integrate import odeint, solve_ivp

from dataclasses import dataclass

from typing import Optional, Tuple, Dict, List

import networkx as nx

@dataclass

class OscillatorParameters:

    """Parameters for individual cellular oscillators"""

    intrinsic_freq: float  # ωᵢ: 10⁻⁵ to 10¹⁴ Hz range

    synaptic_coupling: float  # K: synaptic coupling strength

    field_coupling: float  # ζ: consciousness field coupling

    ephaptic_strength: float  # λ: ephaptic field strength

    noise_amplitude: float  # noise term amplitude

    

class HierarchicalOscillatorNetwork:

    """

    Multilayer Kuramoto Model with Field Coupling

    Implements: dφᵢ/dt = ωᵢ + (K/N)∑ⱼ sin(φⱼ - φᵢ) + ζΨₛcos(φᵢ) + λ∑ₖ Gᵢₖ(φₖ - φᵢ) + ηᵢ(t)

    """

    

    def __init__(self, N: int, topology: str = 'small_world'):

        self.N = N

        self.topology = topology

        self.phases = np.random.uniform(0, 2*np.pi, N)

        self.frequencies = self._initialize_frequencies()

        self.network = self._build_topology()

        self.gap_junction_matrix = self._create_gap_junctions()

        

        # Coupling parameters

        self.params = OscillatorParameters(

            intrinsic_freq=7.83,  # Schumann resonance base

            synaptic_coupling=1.0,

            field_coupling=0.5,

            ephaptic_strength=0.3,

            noise_amplitude=0.1

        )

        

        # Track dynamics

        self.synchronization_history = []

        self.avalanche_sizes = []

        self.metastability_index = []

        

    def _initialize_frequencies(self) -> np.ndarray:

        """Initialize intrinsic frequencies across biological scales"""

        # Multi-scale frequency distribution (log-normal)

        # Ranges from metabolic (10⁻⁵ Hz) to molecular vibrations (10¹⁴ Hz)

        log_freqs = np.random.normal(1, 2, self.N)  # Centered around 10 Hz

        return 10 ** log_freqs

    

    def _build_topology(self) -> nx.Graph:

        """Create network topology (small-world, rich-club, etc.)"""

        if self.topology == 'small_world':

            # Watts-Strogatz small-world network

            G = nx.watts_strogatz_graph(self.N, k=6, p=0.3)

        elif self.topology == 'rich_club':

            # Rich-club topology (hub-based)

            G = nx.barabasi_albert_graph(self.N, m=3)

        elif self.topology == 'modular':

            # Modular network with communities

            G = self._create_modular_network()

        else:

            # Default: random network

            G = nx.erdos_renyi_graph(self.N, p=0.1)

        

        return G

    

    def _create_modular_network(self) -> nx.Graph:

        """Create modular network structure mimicking brain organization"""

        modules = 5  # Number of modules

        module_size = self.N // modules

        G = nx.Graph()

        

        # Create dense modules

        for m in range(modules):

            start = m * module_size

            end = start + module_size

            for i in range(start, end):

                for j in range(i + 1, end):

                    if np.random.random() < 0.6:  # High intra-module connectivity

                        G.add_edge(i, j)

        

        # Add sparse inter-module connections

        for i in range(self.N):

            for j in range(i + 1, self.N):

                if i // module_size != j // module_size:

                    if np.random.random() < 0.05:  # Low inter-module connectivity

                        G.add_edge(i, j)

        

        return G

    

    def _create_gap_junctions(self) -> np.ndarray:

        """Create gap junction conductance matrix"""

        G = np.zeros((self.N, self.N))

        

        # Gap junctions follow network topology with spatial decay

        for edge in self.network.edges():

            i, j = edge

            # Conductance decreases with distance

            distance = np.abs(i - j) / self.N

            G[i, j] = G[j, i] = np.exp(-distance / 0.1)

        

        return G

    

    def kuramoto_dynamics(self, t: float, phases: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:

        """

        Core Kuramoto dynamics with multiple coupling mechanisms

        """

        dphase_dt = np.zeros(self.N)

        

        # Get adjacency matrix

        adj_matrix = nx.adjacency_matrix(self.network).toarray()

        

        for i in range(self.N):

            # Intrinsic frequency

            dphase_dt[i] = self.frequencies[i]

            

            # Synaptic coupling (Kuramoto term)

            neighbors = np.where(adj_matrix[i] > 0)[0]

            if len(neighbors) > 0:

                coupling_sum = np.sum(np.sin(phases[neighbors] - phases[i]))

                dphase_dt[i] += self.params.synaptic_coupling * coupling_sum / len(neighbors)

            

            # Consciousness field coupling

            mean_field = np.mean(np.exp(1j * phases))

            dphase_dt[i] += self.params.field_coupling * np.abs(mean_field) * np.cos(phases[i])

            

            # Gap junction coupling

            gap_coupling = np.sum(self.gap_junction_matrix[i] * (phases - phases[i]))

            dphase_dt[i] += self.params.ephaptic_strength * gap_coupling

            

            # Colored noise

            noise = self.params.noise_amplitude * self._generate_colored_noise()

            dphase_dt[i] += noise

        

        return dphase_dt

    

    def _generate_colored_noise(self) -> float:

        """Generate 1/f colored noise for biological realism"""

        # Simple approximation of 1/f noise

        white = np.random.randn()

        pink = 0.9 * getattr(self, '_prev_noise', 0) + 0.1 * white

        self._prev_noise = pink

        return pink

    

    def calculate_order_parameter(self) -> complex:

        """Calculate Kuramoto order parameter"""

        return np.mean(np.exp(1j * self.phases))

    

    def calculate_synchronization(self) -> float:

        """Calculate global synchronization level"""

        return np.abs(self.calculate_order_parameter())

    

    def detect_avalanches(self, threshold: float = 0.1) -> List[int]:

        """

        Detect neuronal avalanches in the network

        Returns list of avalanche sizes

        """

        # Calculate phase velocities

        velocities = np.gradient(self.phases)

        

        # Identify active sites

        active = np.abs(velocities) > threshold

        

        # Find connected components of active sites

        active_graph = self.network.subgraph(np.where(active)[0])

        components = list(nx.connected_components(active_graph))

        

        avalanche_sizes = [len(comp) for comp in components]

        return avalanche_sizes

    

    def calculate_metastability_index(self, window: int = 100) -> float:

        """

        Calculate metastability index: MI = ⟨(δφ)²⟩/⟨|δφ|⟩²

        Quantifies switching between integrated/segregated states

        """

        if len(self.synchronization_history) < window:

            return 0.0

        

        recent_sync = np.array(self.synchronization_history[-window:])

        fluctuations = recent_sync - np.mean(recent_sync)

        

        numerator = np.mean(fluctuations ** 2)

        denominator = np.mean(np.abs(fluctuations)) ** 2

        

        if denominator > 0:

            return numerator / denominator

        return 0.0

    

    def simulate(self, duration: float, dt: float = 0.001) -> Dict:

        """

        Run simulation and collect metrics

        """

        time_points = np.arange(0, duration, dt)

        

        # Solve ODE

        solution = solve_ivp(

            self.kuramoto_dynamics,

            [0, duration],

            self.phases,

            t_eval=time_points,

            method='RK45'

        )

        

        # Store results

        results = {

            'time': solution.t,

            'phases': solution.y,

            'synchronization': [],

            'avalanches': [],

            'metastability': []

        }

        

        # Calculate metrics at each time point

        for i, t in enumerate(solution.t):

            self.phases = solution.y[:, i]

            

            # Track synchronization

            sync = self.calculate_synchronization()

            results['synchronization'].append(sync)

            self.synchronization_history.append(sync)

            

            # Detect avalanches periodically

            if i % 100 == 0:

                avalanches = self.detect_avalanches()

                self.avalanche_sizes.extend(avalanches)

                results['avalanches'].append(avalanches)

            

            # Calculate metastability

            if i % 10 == 0:

                mi = self.calculate_metastability_index()

                results['metastability'].append(mi)

                self.metastability_index.append(mi)

        

        return results

class QuasicriticalDynamics:

    """

    Implements Griffiths phase dynamics and criticality measures

    """

    

    def __init__(self, network_size: int):

        self.N = network_size

        self.branching_parameter = 1.0  # σ = 1 at criticality

        self.tau_exponent = 1.5  # Power law exponent

        

    def avalanche_distribution(self, sizes: List[int]) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:

        """

        Calculate avalanche size distribution: P(s) ~ s⁻τ exp(-s/s₀)

        """

        if not sizes:

            return np.array([]), np.array([])

        

        # Create histogram

        hist, bins = np.histogram(sizes, bins=50)

        

        # Cutoff scale

        s_cutoff = self.N ** (1 / 1.5)

        

        # Theoretical distribution

        s_values = (bins[:-1] + bins[1:]) / 2

        theoretical = s_values ** (-self.tau_exponent) * np.exp(-s_values / s_cutoff)

        

        return hist, theoretical

    

    def calculate_branching_ratio(self, activity: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Calculate branching parameter σ

        σ > 1: supercritical (e.g., epilepsy)

        σ = 1: critical

        σ < 1: subcritical (e.g., depression)

        """

        descendants = []

        

        for t in range(len(activity) - 1):

            active_now = np.sum(activity[t] > 0)

            active_next = np.sum(activity[t + 1] > 0)

            

            if active_now > 0:

                descendants.append(active_next / active_now)

        

        if descendants:

            return np.mean(descendants)

        return 0.0

    

    def griffiths_phase_detection(self, time_series: np.ndarray) -> Dict:

        """

        Detect Griffiths phase characteristics

        """

        # Calculate autocorrelation

        autocorr = np.correlate(time_series, time_series, mode='full')

        autocorr = autocorr[len(autocorr)//2:]

        

        # Fit power law decay

        x = np.arange(1, len(autocorr) + 1)

        log_x = np.log(x[autocorr > 0])

        log_y = np.log(autocorr[autocorr > 0])

        

        if len(log_x) > 10:

            slope, intercept = np.polyfit(log_x[:100], log_y[:100], 1)

            decay_exponent = -slope

        else:

            decay_exponent = 0.0

        

        # Check for rare regions (local deviations from criticality)

        local_variance = []

        window = 50

        for i in range(0, len(time_series) - window, window):

            local_var = np.var(time_series[i:i+window])

            local_variance.append(local_var)

        

        return {

            'decay_exponent': decay_exponent,

            'is_griffiths': 0.1 < decay_exponent < 1.0,  # Slow decay characteristic

            'heterogeneity': np.std(local_variance) / np.mean(local_variance) if local_variance else 0

        }

class CosmologicalEntrainment:

    """

    Models entrainment with cosmological rhythms

    """

    

    def __init__(self):

        # Schumann resonance frequencies (Hz)

        self.schumann_freqs = [7.83, 14.3, 20.8, 27.3, 33.8]

        

        # Lunar cycle parameters

        self.lunar_period = 29.53  # days

        self.lunar_phase = 0.0

        

        # Circadian parameters

        self.circadian_period = 24.0  # hours

        

    def schumann_resonance_field(self, t: float, location: Tuple[float, float] = (0, 0)) -> np.ndarray:

        """

        Generate Schumann resonance field at time t

        """

        field = np.zeros(len(self.schumann_freqs))

        

        for i, freq in enumerate(self.schumann_freqs):

            # Add geomagnetic modulation

            geomag_modulation = 1.0 + 0.1 * np.sin(2 * np.pi * t / (24 * 3600))

            

            # Amplitude decreases with harmonic number

            amplitude = geomag_modulation / (i + 1)

            

            field[i] = amplitude * np.sin(2 * np.pi * freq * t)

        

        return field

    

    def lunar_influence(self, t_days: float) -> Dict:

        """

        Calculate lunar phase influence on biological rhythms

        """

        # Current lunar phase

        phase = (t_days % self.lunar_period) / self.lunar_period * 2 * np.pi

        

        # Gravitational influence (simplified)

        gravitational = 1.0 + 0.1 * np.cos(phase)

        

        # Electromagnetic influence (subtle)

        electromagnetic = 0.01 * np.sin(phase)

        

        return {

            'phase': phase,

            'gravitational': gravitational,

            'electromagnetic': electromagnetic,

            'illumination': (1 + np.cos(phase)) / 2  # 0 = new moon, 1 = full moon

        }

    

    def circadian_modulation(self, t_hours: float) -> float:

        """

        Circadian rhythm modulation

        """

        phase = (t_hours % self.circadian_period) / self.circadian_period * 2 * np.pi

        

        # Core body temperature rhythm as proxy

        # Minimum at ~4-6 AM, maximum at ~7-9 PM

        return 37.0 + 0.5 * np.sin(phase - np.pi/2)

Multi-Path Coupling Mechanisms and Clinical Biomarkers Extension of SCPN Layer 4 Architecture

"""

Multi-Path Coupling Mechanisms and Clinical Biomarkers

Extension of SCPN Layer 4 Architecture

"""

import numpy as np

import scipy as sp

from scipy import signal, stats, linalg

from scipy.sparse import csr_matrix

from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import warnings

class MultiPathCouplingHamiltonian:

    """

    Implements total coupling Hamiltonian:

    H_total = H_synaptic + H_gap + H_ephaptic + H_glial + H_vascular

    """

    

    def __init__(self, N_neurons: int, N_glia: int, N_vascular: int):

        self.N_neurons = N_neurons

        self.N_glia = N_glia

        self.N_vascular = N_vascular

        

        # Initialize coupling matrices

        self.J_synaptic = self._initialize_synaptic_matrix()

        self.g_gap = self._initialize_gap_junctions()

        

        # Field parameters

        self.epsilon_0 = 8.854e-12  # Permittivity of free space

        self.tissue_permittivity = 80  # Relative permittivity of brain tissue

        

        # State variables

        self.neuron_states = np.random.randn(N_neurons)

        self.glia_calcium = np.random.uniform(50, 200, N_glia)  # nM

        self.blood_flow = np.random.uniform(40, 60, N_vascular)  # ml/100g/min

        

    def _initialize_synaptic_matrix(self) -> np.ndarray:

        """Initialize synaptic coupling matrix with Dale's law"""

        J = np.random.randn(self.N_neurons, self.N_neurons) * 0.1

        

        # Enforce Dale's law: 80% excitatory, 20% inhibitory

        n_excitatory = int(0.8 * self.N_neurons)

        J[:n_excitatory, :] = np.abs(J[:n_excitatory, :])

        J[n_excitatory:, :] = -np.abs(J[n_excitatory:, :])

        

        # Remove self-connections

        np.fill_diagonal(J, 0)

        

        return J

    

    def _initialize_gap_junctions(self) -> np.ndarray:

        """Initialize gap junction conductances"""

        g = np.zeros((self.N_neurons, self.N_neurons))

        

        # Gap junctions primarily between inhibitory neurons

        n_excitatory = int(0.8 * self.N_neurons)

        for i in range(n_excitatory, self.N_neurons):

            for j in range(i + 1, self.N_neurons):

                if np.random.random() < 0.3:  # 30% connection probability

                    conductance = np.random.uniform(0.1, 1.0)  # nS

                    g[i, j] = g[j, i] = conductance

        

        return g

    

    def H_synaptic(self, sigma: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Chemical synaptic Hamiltonian: H_synaptic = -∑ᵢⱼ Jᵢⱼ σᵢσⱼ

        """

        return -0.5 * np.sum(sigma @ self.J_synaptic @ sigma)

    

    def H_gap(self, V: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Gap junction Hamiltonian: H_gap = -∑⟨ij⟩ gᵢⱼ(Vᵢ - Vⱼ)²

        """

        energy = 0

        for i in range(self.N_neurons):

            for j in range(i + 1, self.N_neurons):

                if self.g_gap[i, j] > 0:

                    energy -= self.g_gap[i, j] * (V[i] - V[j]) ** 2

        return energy

    

    def H_ephaptic(self, E_field: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Ephaptic field Hamiltonian: H_ephaptic = -∫ ε₀|E|²/2 dV

        """

        # Simplified: discrete sum over field points

        epsilon = self.epsilon_0 * self.tissue_permittivity

        return -0.5 * epsilon * np.sum(np.abs(E_field) ** 2)

    

    def H_glial(self, Ca_concentration: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Glial calcium wave Hamiltonian: H_glial = -∑ₖ αₖ[Ca²⁺]ₖ

        """

        # Alpha represents calcium-dependent energy

        alpha = 0.01  # Coupling constant

        return -alpha * np.sum(Ca_concentration)

    

    def H_vascular(self, flow: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Hemodynamic coupling Hamiltonian: H_vascular = -∑ᵥ βᵥ(flow)ᵥ

        """

        beta = 0.1  # Neurovascular coupling constant

        return -beta * np.sum(flow)

    

    def total_hamiltonian(self) -> float:

        """Calculate total system Hamiltonian"""

        # Generate field from current neural states

        E_field = self._calculate_electric_field(self.neuron_states)

        

        H_total = (

            self.H_synaptic(self.neuron_states) +

            self.H_gap(self.neuron_states * 70)  # Convert to mV

            + self.H_ephaptic(E_field)

            + self.H_glial(self.glia_calcium)

            + self.H_vascular(self.blood_flow)

        )

        

        return H_total

    

    def _calculate_electric_field(self, neural_states: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:

        """

        Calculate electric field from neural activity

        Simplified: field proportional to local neural activity gradient

        """

        # Create spatial arrangement

        grid_size = int(np.sqrt(self.N_neurons))

        if grid_size ** 2 < self.N_neurons:

            grid_size += 1

        

        # Pad states to fit grid

        padded_states = np.zeros(grid_size ** 2)

        padded_states[:self.N_neurons] = neural_states

        

        # Reshape to 2D grid

        grid = padded_states.reshape(grid_size, grid_size)

        

        # Calculate gradient (electric field)

        E_y, E_x = np.gradient(grid)

        E_field = np.sqrt(E_x ** 2 + E_y ** 2).flatten()[:self.N_neurons]

        

        return E_field

    

    def evolve_system(self, dt: float = 0.001) -> None:

        """Evolve the coupled system forward in time"""

        # Neural dynamics

        dS_dt = -np.gradient(self.total_hamiltonian())

        self.neuron_states += dS_dt * dt

        

        # Glial calcium dynamics (simplified)

        # Calcium waves propagate through gap junctions

        Ca_diffusion = 0.1  # Diffusion constant

        for i in range(self.N_glia):

            # Simple diffusion to neighbors

            if i > 0:

                self.glia_calcium[i] += Ca_diffusion * (self.glia_calcium[i-1] - self.glia_calcium[i]) * dt

            if i < self.N_glia - 1:

                self.glia_calcium[i] += Ca_diffusion * (self.glia_calcium[i+1] - self.glia_calcium[i]) * dt

        

        # Neurovascular coupling

        # Blood flow follows neural activity with delay

        tau_neurovasc = 1.0  # seconds

        target_flow = 40 + 20 * np.mean(np.abs(self.neuron_states))

        self.blood_flow += (target_flow - self.blood_flow) * dt / tau_neurovasc

class ClinicalBiomarkers:

    """

    Clinical biomarkers for consciousness states

    """

    

    def __init__(self):

        self.biomarkers = {}

        

    def phase_locking_value(self, signals: np.ndarray, freq_band: Tuple[float, float] = (8, 12)) -> float:

        """

        Calculate Phase Locking Value (PLV) for given frequency band

        High PLV indicates strong phase synchronization

        """

        n_signals, n_samples = signals.shape

        

        # Bandpass filter

        fs = 1000  # Sampling frequency (Hz)

        nyquist = fs / 2

        low = freq_band[0] / nyquist

        high = freq_band[1] / nyquist

        

        # Avoid filter issues

        if low <= 0 or high >= 1:

            return 0.0

        

        b, a = signal.butter(4, [low, high], btype='band')

        

        # Filter signals and extract phase

        phases = np.zeros_like(signals)

        for i in range(n_signals):

            filtered = signal.filtfilt(b, a, signals[i])

            analytic = signal.hilbert(filtered)

            phases[i] = np.angle(analytic)

        

        # Calculate PLV between all pairs

        plv_values = []

        for i in range(n_signals):

            for j in range(i + 1, n_signals):

                phase_diff = phases[i] - phases[j]

                plv = np.abs(np.mean(np.exp(1j * phase_diff)))

                plv_values.append(plv)

        

        return np.mean(plv_values) if plv_values else 0.0

    

    def weighted_phase_lag_index(self, signals: np.ndarray) -> float:

        """

        Calculate weighted Phase Lag Index (wPLI)

        Robust to volume conduction effects

        """

        n_signals, n_samples = signals.shape

        

        # Calculate cross-spectral density

        nperseg = min(256, n_samples // 4)

        freqs, csd = signal.csd(signals[0], signals[0], fs=1000, nperseg=nperseg)

        

        wpli_matrix = np.zeros((n_signals, n_signals))

        

        for i in range(n_signals):

            for j in range(i + 1, n_signals):

                _, Cxy = signal.csd(signals[i], signals[j], fs=1000, nperseg=nperseg)

                

                # Imaginary part of cross-spectrum

                imag_csd = np.imag(Cxy)

                

                # wPLI calculation

                numerator = np.abs(np.mean(imag_csd))

                denominator = np.mean(np.abs(imag_csd))

                

                if denominator > 0:

                    wpli_matrix[i, j] = numerator / denominator

        

        return np.mean(wpli_matrix[wpli_matrix > 0])

    

    def criticality_markers(self, activity: np.ndarray) -> Dict:

        """

        Calculate markers of criticality

        σ branching parameter: =1 critical, >1 supercritical, <1 subcritical

        """

        markers = {}

        

        # Branching parameter

        branching_ratios = []

        for t in range(len(activity) - 1):

            active_now = np.sum(activity[t] > 0)

            active_next = np.sum(activity[t + 1] > 0)

            if active_now > 0:

                branching_ratios.append(active_next / active_now)

        

        markers['branching_parameter'] = np.mean(branching_ratios) if branching_ratios else 0.0

        

        # Determine state

        sigma = markers['branching_parameter']

        if sigma > 1.1:

            markers['state'] = 'supercritical'

            markers['clinical_correlate'] = 'epilepsy_risk'

        elif sigma < 0.9:

            markers['state'] = 'subcritical'

            markers['clinical_correlate'] = 'depression_risk'

        else:

            markers['state'] = 'critical'

            markers['clinical_correlate'] = 'healthy'

        

        # Long-range temporal correlations (DFA)

        markers['dfa_exponent'] = self._detrended_fluctuation_analysis(activity.flatten())

        

        return markers

    

    def _detrended_fluctuation_analysis(self, time_series: np.ndarray, scales: Optional[np.ndarray] = None) -> float:

        """

        Detrended Fluctuation Analysis (DFA) for long-range correlations

        Returns scaling exponent (0.5 = white noise, 1.0 = 1/f noise)

        """

        if scales is None:

            scales = np.logspace(1, 3, 20, dtype=int)

        

        # Integrate time series

        y = np.cumsum(time_series - np.mean(time_series))

        

        fluctuations = []

        for scale in scales:

            if scale >= len(y):

                continue

                

            # Divide into segments

            n_segments = len(y) // scale

            

            if n_segments == 0:

                continue

            

            segment_vars = []

            for i in range(n_segments):

                segment = y[i * scale:(i + 1) * scale]

                

                # Detrend with linear fit

                x = np.arange(len(segment))

                coeffs = np.polyfit(x, segment, 1)

                trend = np.poly1d(coeffs)(x)

                

                # Calculate fluctuation

                segment_var = np.sqrt(np.mean((segment - trend) ** 2))

                segment_vars.append(segment_var)

            

            fluctuations.append(np.mean(segment_vars))

        

        if len(fluctuations) > 2:

            # Fit power law

            valid_scales = scales[:len(fluctuations)]

            log_scales = np.log(valid_scales)

            log_fluct = np.log(fluctuations)

            

            # Linear regression in log-log space

            alpha, _ = np.polyfit(log_scales, log_fluct, 1)

            return alpha

        

        return 0.5  # Default to white noise

    

    def pathological_detection(self, neural_data: np.ndarray) -> Dict:

        """

        Detect pathological states from neural dynamics

        """

        detections = {}

        

        # Calculate biomarkers

        plv = self.phase_locking_value(neural_data)

        wpli = self.weighted_phase_lag_index(neural_data)

        criticality = self.criticality_markers(neural_data)

        

        # Epilepsy detection

        if criticality['branching_parameter'] > 1.2:

            detections['epilepsy_risk'] = 'high'

            detections['recommendation'] = 'Consider anti-epileptic intervention'

        

        # Depression detection

        if criticality['branching_parameter'] < 0.8 and plv < 0.3:

            detections['depression_markers'] = 'present'

            detections['recommendation'] = 'Evaluate for mood disorders'

        

        # Schizophrenia markers

        if wpli < 0.2 and criticality['dfa_exponent'] < 0.6:

            detections['schizophrenia_markers'] = 'present'

            detections['recommendation'] = 'Assess connectivity disruption'

        

        # Consciousness level

        consciousness_score = (plv + wpli + (1 - abs(1 - criticality['branching_parameter']))) / 3

        

        if consciousness_score > 0.7:

            detections['consciousness_level'] = 'fully_conscious'

        elif consciousness_score > 0.4:

            detections['consciousness_level'] = 'altered_consciousness'

        else:

            detections['consciousness_level'] = 'minimal_consciousness'

        

        detections['biomarker_values'] = {

            'PLV': plv,

            'wPLI': wpli,

            'branching_parameter': criticality['branching_parameter'],

            'DFA_exponent': criticality['dfa_exponent']

        }

        

        return detections

class TherapeuticInterventions:

    """

    Therapeutic intervention protocols based on tissue synchronization

    """

    

    def __init__(self):

        self.protocols = {}

        

    def transcranial_stimulation_protocol(self, 

                                         target_frequency: float,

                                         current_state: str) -> Dict:

        """

        Design transcranial stimulation protocol

        """

        protocol = {

            'type': 'tACS',  # Transcranial Alternating Current Stimulation

            'frequency': target_frequency,

            'intensity': 2.0,  # mA

            'duration': 20,  # minutes

            'electrode_montage': 'F3-F4',  # Frontal sites

        }

        

        # Adjust based on pathological state

        if current_state == 'epilepsy_risk':

            # Reduce excitability

            protocol['type'] = 'tDCS'  # Direct current

            protocol['polarity'] = 'cathodal'

            protocol['intensity'] = 1.0

            

        elif current_state == 'depression_risk':

            # Increase excitability

            protocol['frequency'] = 10.0  # Alpha frequency

            protocol['intensity'] = 2.5

            protocol['electrode_montage'] = 'F3-Fp2'  # Left DLPFC

            

        elif current_state == 'schizophrenia_markers':

            # Enhance gamma synchronization

            protocol['frequency'] = 40.0  # Gamma

            protocol['intensity'] = 1.5

            

        return protocol

    

    def pharmacological_modulation(self, biomarkers: Dict) -> List[str]:

        """

        Suggest pharmacological interventions based on criticality

        """

        suggestions = []

        

        branching = biomarkers.get('branching_parameter', 1.0)

        

        if branching > 1.1:

            # Supercritical - reduce excitation

            suggestions.append("GABAergic enhancement (e.g., benzodiazepines)")

            suggestions.append("Sodium channel blockers (e.g., carbamazepine)")

            

        elif branching < 0.9:

            # Subcritical - increase excitation

            suggestions.append("NMDA receptor modulation (e.g., ketamine)")

            suggestions.append("Monoamine enhancement (e.g., SSRIs)")

            

        # Based on synchronization

        if biomarkers.get('PLV', 0) < 0.3:

            suggestions.append("Cholinergic enhancement for attention")

            

        if biomarkers.get('wPLI', 0) < 0.2:

            suggestions.append("Dopaminergic modulation for connectivity")

            

        return suggestions

    

    def circadian_rhythm_intervention(self, current_phase: float) -> Dict:

        """

        Design circadian rhythm intervention

        """

        optimal_phase = np.pi  # Noon

        phase_shift = optimal_phase - current_phase

        

        intervention = {

            'light_therapy': {

                'timing': 'morning' if phase_shift > 0 else 'evening',

                'intensity': 10000,  # lux

                'duration': 30,  # minutes

                'wavelength': 480  # nm (blue light)

            },

            'melatonin': {

                'dose': 3,  # mg

                'timing': 'evening' if phase_shift > 0 else 'avoid'

            },

            'activity_schedule': {

                'exercise': 'morning' if phase_shift > 0 else 'afternoon',

                'meals': 'regular times, avoid late eating'

            }

        }

        

        return intervention

# Example usage and testing

if __name__ == "__main__":
